_Design_ _**Tip** #18:_ Likewise, never end page 1 of a sales letter with a period. When someone is reading your letter and he or she is at the bottom of page 1, it's a "critical commitment moment," when they decide whether to buy into reading the rest of the letter or put the whole thing aside for a later time, which of course is an advertisement's death sentence. 

End page 1 with some sort of cliffhanger—a thought about to be completed, a mystery solved, a question answered, a story finished, or at the very least a sentence finished on page 2. Just arrange your text so that you end page 1 in midsentence, forcing the thought—and the reader—to continue on page 2. 

_Design_ _**Tip** #19:_ Photos should have captions. Readers look for them. You want to design your ad or direct mail letter to match your audience's reading habits. And one habit that most people have is to look for a caption under a photograph. Whenever you have an especially interesting photo, one that seems to be telling a story, it's a wasted sales opportunity if you don't have an interesting caption under it. You've used excellent ammunition to bring your reader's attention to this visual, 

- 4 3 5 - 

so what are you going to do with it? Don't waste the opportunity. Use it to sell a feature-and-benefit combination or something else that arises from the photograph. 

_**Design Tip** #20:_ Every letter, for the same reason, should end with at least one PS because studies have shown the PS is the second-most highly read part of any letter, second only to the headline. Direct marketers have studied, watching through two-way mirrors, how people open and read direct mail. Usually they'll open it up, spread the pieces around, look for the letter and read the headline, and often flip to the back to see if there's a PS. Here, too, if you don't have one, you're missing a great opportunity to sell. 

These studies also showed that after looking everything over, many people will head straight for the order form. This was surprising to many direct marketing pros, because we all assumed that this would be looked at last, when someone is ready to order. Not so! Our audience is so much smarter than we give them credit for. When asked about this behavior, one of the people being watched expressed the reason for this common but previously unobserved behavior. He said, "Oh, sure. I always go to the order form after I've looked everything over. _On the order form is where they sum up the deal."_ 

This means you should always design your order form to be a miniature version of the ad, summarizing the strongest benefits of your product and offer. _**Design Tip #21:**_ Don't kill widows; they are the breath of life. I'm not speaking about the widows we were talking about earlier, the ones who sell insurance in Japan! Widows are the little bits of type at the end of a paragraph, usually a single word that happens to fall on its own line. 

Like pedantic schoolmarms, some editors pounce on these defenseless creatures as if they were enemies of the state to be dragged off and executed. 

The great advertising man Fairfax Cone said this attitude is wrong. Let widows be. Hone your writing as tightly as you can, and let the widows fall where they may. They give a little extra air to a layout, a refreshing breath of life, so let them be. 

Since the days of Fairfax Cone, others have done readership studies that confirm his commonsense observation. Long pieces of copy where the widows were left alone had slightly higher readership than layouts where everything was tight in chockablock form. 

In my own writing, I don't worry about them either way. I'm not going to try to create them or get rid of them. If the sentence is well written, I don't want to artificially cut it down or balloon it out because of a widow. 

- 4 3 6 - 

_**Design Tip #22:**_ Use subheads as recharging stations to boost flagging interest. All the skill that you've put into writing a headline should also be harnessed to write subheads, which keep refreshing a reader's flagging interest. Subheads also serve to arrest the interest of the quick-skim artist who thought he might escape with a fast "once-over-then-toss." Subheads put many more "baited hooks" dangling in the water. 

_**Design Tip #23:**_ Keep your paragraphs to five or six lines. If that means you've got to interrupt a thought where you shouldn't, you can let the paragraph go a little longer, but not too much. 

_**Design Tip #24:**_ When your product is a conceptual one, you will normally make your headline the main thought, the first big impression. 

But some products demand dominant visuals. If you're selling beautiful artwork or jewelry or collectible plates or crystal glass or Persian rugs or a cottage by the lake, you should at least test an ad with a beautiful visual of what you're selling. 

In the example before, where we were selling a book on looking younger, I believe it boosted response significantly to show beautiful women looking so much younger than their actual age. They became the stars of the mailing. 

As a copywriter, you normally think in words, trying to construct persuasive headlines and sentences. But always remember to investigate the visual possibilities. This will open up whole new possibilities to you. Sometimes the right visual will deliver an immediacy and impact that words simply cannot match. When you combine such a potent visual with compelling words, you may well hit a grand slam. 

Always ask, "How can we bring in visuals that dramatically reinforce the selling message?" And for some products, once you raise that question, you realize that a dramatic visual should _dominate_ the message. 

_Design_ _**Tip** #25:_ In most direct mail packages, the letter is the beating heart of the mailing. Direct mail has always been called the most personal advertising medium because letters have a more personal impact on people than do mass messages on TV, radio, or in newspapers and magazines. A letter is one person writing to another person, one on one. It's the heart of the message in every sense of the word. 

This is why, even in magalogs, bookalogs, and other formats where there is no separate letter, I always include a letter within the format itself, usually beginning in the first spread. 

- 437 - 

Interestingly, a traditional direct mail package, say a #10 envelope package, will often pull a _lower_ response when it includes a brochure. 

This seems counterintuitive, as many copywriters were once taught to always include both—to use the letter for the more personal "sell" copy and highlight the "features and photographs" in the brochure. That is still a common formula. 

What's wrong with that? Why would a brochure often (though not always) _depress_ response? 

Remember what I said before—the eye is drawn to pictures first. When potential customers open the direct mail package, after quickly scanning the contents and deciding this could be something of interest, they'll pick one piece to start reading first. At that point, they'll be drawn to the photos of the brochure first, pick it up, and start reading. And that's exactly the _wrong_ thing you want your reader to look at first, because a brochure screams "sales pitch," is usually "feature" driven (not benefit driven), and lacks that one-on-one feeling you can create in a letter. 

So beware if you hear a copy chief or marketing director say, "I need a letter and a brochure" for such and such a product." You might want to test that combination, because I've often seen a colorful brochure depress response. 

Look at it this way. In the history of direct marketing, there have been countless thousands of extremely successful packages with nothing more than an envelope, a letter, and an order form. But in 40 years in direct marketing, I've never seen a single successful direct mail package—not one!—consisting of a brochure but no sales letter. Maybe there have been a few, but I've never seen any. 

_**Design Tip** #26:_ Make sure your letter emerges from the envelope face forward, with your headline above the fold. I hear some of you laughing, perhaps relating to that message. How often do you spend so much time crafting an important, powerful headline, and the printer inserts the letter so that the first thing the reader sees upon pulling out the contents of the envelope is a hodgepodge of upside down type? Or even worse, a blank panel? (I hate blank panels—wasted selling space!) 

Always assume that your reader will open your letter from the rear of the envelope, as that's where the flap is. As soon as he pulls out the contents, he should be seeing the headline of the letter facing him. This is very important. 

That's such a bugaboo with me because you can work so hard to make that message come in exactly the right place at exactly the right moment and then the production people just put it in backwards, and the person has to fumble around to get to the beginning of your letter. Maybe they don't feel like fumbling with your mail. Maybe they're too pressed for time to reassemble your mail the way it should 

- 4 3 8 - 

have gone out, to do the job your printer should have. In either case, the sale is lost. 

_Design Tip #27:_ This is a great one—make sure your response device fits inside your return envelope! Did you ever have to respond with a little envelope and a giant order form? _Arghh!_ 

You fold it up and stuff it in. So far, so good. You lick the envelope, but the envelope is bulging and the glue isn't strong enough to hold. The envelope flap pops open, and of course you wouldn't want your mailman to discover that you're sending for a product to enhance your sex life or make beer in your basement. 

So you try to reseal the envelope; only now the glue is even weaker. You reach into your desk for Scotch® tape and remember that your daughter borrowed it for school, and you say, "Ah, the heck with this stupid thing. I didn't really need it anyway," and you toss it. Mismatched order forms and envelopes have cost many a sale. 

_Design Tip #28:_ Make sure your address and contact information are on every piece in the package. So often people will throw away every piece but one. They'll think, "I'm going to order this later, so I'll save this one piece of the package." But when later comes, they realize, "Oh, my goodness, there's no phone number on this paper. There's no place to order, no company name, nothing. Oh, well, I'll order it next time." And "next time" may never come. _Every single piece in a direct mail package should have the information of where to contact you._ 

_Design Tip #29:_ Always look at your advertising the same way your prospects will. This was a very interesting thing that Ogilvy taught us. 

He said that the following course of events is both common and tragic. The agency's creative people brainstorm a new campaign for a client, then mock up their best headline concepts on storyboards for client approval. 

These mock-ups will normally show the headline, main visuals, and other major elements of each proposed ad so the client can judge the main ideas. 

Then the team schedules a big meeting with the client to present these ideas. The only problem is, the client will be reviewing these mock-ups in a different setting than the eventual prospects. 

In other words, at the meeting where these ads will be reviewed, it's usually in a big boardroom, with quite a few people attending. 

The ad agency wants to be sure that everyone can read the headlines, so they create layouts that can be read from 20 feet away, by someone sitting at the far end of the conference-room table. 

- 4 3 9 - 

The clients then select the ads they like best, the agency people go back to their offices, and everyone's happy, because the client approved several of the ads. Then the copywriters race to "fill in" the blanks of the ads so they can be run. Nobody wants to change the layouts now, because the client has approved them. 

So you wind up with layouts and headline type sizes that were originally meant to be read 20 feet away now being printed in newspapers that are read from only inches away. And that's why you will often see monstrosities like this... 

**==> picture [432 x 520] intentionally omitted <==**

Anyone reading this in a newspaper has to almost step back to comprehend a headline in such large type. 

Headlines like this are written for people sitting around a boardroom, not for people riding on a train. But because the client approved it, the agency runs with it, and a terrible waste of money and effort ensues. 

The solution: always, always take your proposed ad, cut it out, and paste it in the actual medium where it will run. This sobering exercise will open your eyes and let you judge your ad just as your reader will. 

You can do the same thing in direct mail. Mock up an envelope and letter and stick it in a typical pile of mail you're likely to receive on a heavy mail day. 

Does it stand out? Does it offer enough immediate value in exchange for a reading? Is it good enough for you to stop what you're doing in your busy day and read through it all? 

Tough tests, to be sure. But these are the tests of reality, the tests your prospect will impose regardless of your fondest hopes. So do a dry run on yourself...and be prepared to make improvements once you see your work in the same harsh light your prospect will! 

**==> picture [185 x 16] intentionally omitted <==**

- 441 - 

**==> picture [565 x 223] intentionally omitted <==**

_GARYBENCIVENGA:_ This is a session very dear to my heart. It's called _Mastering the Alchemy of Desire._ 

This is what we are as marketers and copywriters—masters of desire. We are people who work with the desires of the human heart, and it helps a great deal if you can understand how desires work in your own mind and heart, and how to fulfill them for yourself. This will make you much more effective in influencing the hearts of others. 

So we're going to look at this whole subject of desire and how you can become a master of it, someone who knows how to intensify desire, clarify it, fulfill it in your own life and in the lives of the people you wish to influence. 

Richard, would you like to help us with our introduction? We have a poem, a poem about desire, and I thought it would be a fitting way to start this session. I am going to invite my good friend Richard Stanton-Jones to read this poem, so you won't have to endure my Brooklyn accent. 

_Richard Stanton-Jones:_ Thank you, Gary. This is "Fire and Ice" by Robert Frost. _(RICHARD READS POEM.)_ 

**==> picture [402 x 254] intentionally omitted <==**

GARY BENCIVENGA: Bravo, Richard! 

_(APPLAUSE)_ 

_GARY BENCIVENGA:_ Our new Richard Burton has emerged! 

- 445 - 

Since we are copywriters and marketers, I think that the line I like best in that poem is, _"From what I've tasted of desire, I hold with those who favor fire."_ 

This is such a important topic because _as within, so without._ When you are much more familiar with your own feelings, what motivates you, and you pay attention to those feelings during your daily activities, you get a much better understanding for the same process that goes on in others. 

Let me mention a few things about desire, getting some help from the brilliant modern economist, Paul Zane Pilzer. I'm going to start by putting up a picture of another economist, John Maynard Keynes, who was famous in the early 1900s. 

**==> picture [260 x 195] intentionally omitted <==**

Keynes was a world-renowned economist who helped President Franklin Delano Roosevelt get America back on track during the Great Depression. During those dark years, in the 1930s, the government was trying desperately to pull the economy out of its terrible tailspin, and Keynes advised President Roosevelt on how to do this. 

FDR asked Lord Keynes if he was sure his ideas were going to work. America had never faced such tough economic times. Much of the nation was out of work. Bad weather was turning the Midwest into a dust bowl, putting many farms out of business. In cities, professional people were selling apples on street corners. Breadlines and soup lines were forming everywhere across the nation, and despair gripped millions of families. 

Lord Keynes responded with the utmost confidence. He told the president not to worry, that we were already seeing the strength of the economy coming back. The results were not apparent immediately, but the economy was already on the 

446 - 

mend. In fact, what Keynes saw as we moved forward was that the U.S. and other industrial nations would see a serious problem arising from how _strong_ their economies would grow. 

FDR asked, "How so?" 

Lord Keynes explained that though you can't see the improvements yet, you will in a short time. In fact, almost every person in America who wants a job will eventually have one. There will be food on everyone's table. And nearly all workers will be able to own their own homes. There will be indoor electricity and plumbing throughout the country. And we would have a very, very strong economy. 

And the president wondered, "So what's the problem?" Keynes said, "Here's the problem. Once you _satisfy_ all these basic desires of people, they may never again want to work hard." 

And this was Keynes' real worry—that once people's basic economic desires were satisfied, they would grow lazy and not have burning desires anymore. 

Well, the good economist Lord Keynes may have known a lot about the economy, but he didn't really know enough about the human heart, because desires are _infinite_ and _never ending._ In fact, you could argue that we are now more prosperous than any people in the history of the world, yet we are working as hard as ever. That's because desires are infinite and never ending. 

## **The Nature of Desires** 

In fact, here's a list of what I know about desires from my own experience as well as from economist Paul Zane Pilzer, author of _God Wants You to Be Rich._ 

_1. Desires are infinite in variety._ Have you ever had the experience that you want _everything_ life has to offer? I'm sure you have, as this is the human condition. Our desires are infinite. We want it all! Lord Keynes never had to worry. Desires are infinite and never ending, which is a blessing for us marketers! 

_2. Desires are replaced almost as soon as fulfilled._ I'm sure you've also had this experience—you wanted something so badly, your whole world seemed to revolve around it. You could never be truly happy without possessing this object of your desire. And what happened once it was yours? In a day, a week, or a month, you wanted something else! That's because desires are replaced almost as soon as fulfilled. 

_3. Desires are hard to create but easier to intensify._ This is what we were discussing before. It's usually very poor marketing to attempt to educate somebody into wanting the type of product you offer. For example, if someone isn't already 

- 447 - 

in the market for a new car, you're wasting your effort trying to sell them first on buying a new car, then on buying your specific make, and finally on buying now. That's three big sales to make, and your odds are very slim. Far better to start by talking to people already hot to buy a new car, then intensifying and channeling their preexisting desire into what you offer. This one little insight will save you untold amounts of money and grief if your inclination is to try to persuade people to buy something they don't already want. 

_**4. Desires evolve from "quantity" into "quality."**_ As Pilzer points out, when you're first out of school and you land your first real job, you buy a suit. You'll get a decent suit, but you don't have a lot of money to spend, so it will be a basic offthe-rack suit. Then as your career starts, you say to yourself, "I can't wear this one suit all the time. I need a few." At this stage, you're into _quantity_ suit purchases. 

But after a while, when you visit your favorite clothing store, the salesperson says to you, "Just try on this Brioni suit. It just came in, and it's gorgeous." You say, "No, please, that's beyond my means." 

The salesperson insists, "Just try the jacket on for size. I want you to see what a great Italian suit feels like, how handsomely the silk drapes over your shoulders." 

You try it on; you look in the mirror and think, "Wow! I look like a million bucks, don't I?" 

Soon thereafter, you have in mind that someday you're going to own a Brioni or Armani or Zegna fine suit that you can be so proud of. The seed of desire has been planted, and someday you _do_ make that quality purchase and feel so good about it. 

This is the natural evolution of desire, from _quantity_ to _quality,_ and it holds true for cars, computers, or suits. 

I'm sure the car that you want today is not the same car as when you were in school. It's no longer basic transportation. You want a different car today, one that expresses your sense of style, your values, or needs at this stage in your life. 

You've moved up from being the "quantity" or "basic commodity" purchaser to a higher level of quality that matches your evolving and ever-rising level of desire. 

It's like chocolate. I know we have some chocoholics in the audience. No names will be mentioned, of course! When we were young and trick-or-treating, we may have fallen in love with Hershey's Kisses. Then one year, for your birthday, someone gave you a box of Godiva chocolates, and your standard of desiring was raised. 

- 4 4 8 - 

And then you come to this seminar and you go to the store across the street, called Richart, where you encounter some of the finest chocolatiers in the world. You might have to take out a second mortgage to buy some of their chocolates, but once you do, you'll never be satisfied with any other chocolate again unless it's on the same level. Do try to visit them, by the way. They have utterly indescribable chocolates. 

And that's how your desire evolves. It goes from quantity to ever-greater levels of quality. 

As a marketer, what does this mean to you? 

It means that _there is usually a better, higher-quality, higher-priced version of your product that you can create and offer to your customers, and they will gobble it up because their standard of desiring is always evolving higher._ 

There is almost always a growing portion of your customer base waiting for the next jump in improvement, and they will pay you handsomely for giving it to them. Of course, they do expect your $20 chocolates to taste better than Hershey's Kisses. But give them a "wow" experience, and price resistance melts like a bonbon on your tongue. 

**5.** _**Desires also evolve from the general to the more specialized.**_ This may be the most important point that we should bear in mind as marketers. 

When IBM had a near monopoly on mainframe computers, soon thereafter the market started specializing. This is inevitable in every field. As more and more customers enter a market, their needs become more and more specialized and, once a critical mass is reached where many customers need the same specialized version of a product, some enterprising entrepreneur will realize that and provide a more specialized version for that growing subgroup of customers. 

If you're not aware of this, you very often miss the train as it leaves the station—the train that's heading for the next hot new product. You have to keep a close eye on when the market you're in now is ready to subdivide into two different markets or four different markets. Once you know this principle, you can apply it to launch great new products—and grow fabulously wealthy—by bringing to market exactly the right product just as the market is about to subdivide. 

For example, first there were mainframe computers. And then somebody figured out that there are a lot of businesses needing computers out in the branch offices of major companies, not just in the home office where the mainframes sit and spit out paper. Let's create a _network computer_ so these branch offices can hook into the home-office database. 

- 449 - 

In time, the computer market subdivided again. In all those branch offices, everyone could be more productive with a computer, instead of just the branch manager. So let's offer them _desktops,_ which became another huge market. 

And so it went with each new subdivision of desire. Just as the desire for a branch-office network computer _subdivided_ into desires for individual desktop computers, so, too, the business community's desire for desktops subdivided into desires for laptops, notebooks, handhelds, PDAs, and, in fact, thousands and thousands of specialized computers that are now embedded in all kinds of specialized machinery in medicine, manufacturing, printing, and every other industry. 

Hot new software products developed in the same way. First there were a few master database programs, and then more specialized markets desired more specialized versions. This process continues in almost all markets _endlessly._ 

You can apply this as a general rule and make a great deal of money... 

## **Desires Always Subdivide from the More General to the More Specialized, and So, Therefore, Do Red-Hot New Product Categories** 

Whatever product category you're in, always keep an eye on how your product or service may subdivide next, and you can easily be first to come out with a hot new product. Always ask yourself, _"How is the demand for my current product most likely to subdivide next? If that does in fact happen, how could we satisfy that specialized demand with a more specialized version of our current product? "_ 

We looked at computers. Let's take vitamins as another example. The mass market for vitamins started with one-a-day vitamins that were for everybody. 

Then as more people started buying supplements, they were ready for more specialized offerings, and the marketplace subdivided into men's vitamins, children's vitamins, women's vitamins, and so on. 

Take sneakers. When I was growing up, your mom took you to the shoe store to buy a plain old pair of sneakers. 

But over the years, this marketplace subdivided into specialized shoes for tennis, hiking, walking, running, basketball, sprinting, you name it. 

If you're a runner and you go into the athletic shoe store—simply because marketers have been sensitive to these specializations and the subdivisions within their product categories—you will not accept, if you're a runner, anything but 

- 4 5 0 - 

## "runners shoes." 

You wouldn't dream of getting a basketball sneaker, even though they could be virtually identical in how they function. Because there is now a specialized category of shoes for runners, you won't accept anything but that. And, though I'm not a runner anymore, I'll bet that even within runners shoes, you can now find subdivisions—more specialized runners shoes for marathoners, sprinters, middledistance runners, who knows? 

What does this mean to you as a marketer? 

It means that if you're the first marketer to spot a major new _subdivision of desire_ about to erupt, you can make a killing by having a specialized product to offer this subdividing market. Your new, more specialized product can in fact become the catalyst and major beneficiary of a whole new, more specialized product category. 

If you're the first on the scene with a product that matches the emerging subdivision in the market's desire, the mere specialization of your product, all by itself, almost closes the sale for you and can win a legion of new adherents. 

Look at how easy it is to sell when you have a more specialized product that a big hunk of your market is now ready for... 

Let's say I was a runner back in the day when the only "athletic shoes" were "POS"—plain old sneakers. 

But on this fateful day when I walk into the shoe store to buy my plain old sneakers, the salesman asks, _"What will you be using these for? "_ 

"I'm a runner," I respond. "I run to get exercise." 

He says, "Glad I asked. You know what they've just come out with?" 

I ask, "What?" 

He says, _"Runners_ shoes." 

## I say, _"Runners shoes?"_

He responds, "Yeah. Lemme show ya." 

From that fateful moment on, no great headline, no compelling body copy, no fantastic premium or tempting offer will be needed for me to want these new runners shoes more than I ever wanted plain old sneakers. _The mere fact of specialization, the subdividing of a general product category into a new product that suits my more specialized desire, is all I need to want those runners shoes above all other "sneakers " and never be satisfied with anything else, unless it's a further specialization that repeats the process anew._ 

- 451 - 

Because of the mere existence of runners shoes, I'll never again want to settle for plain old sneakers. I'm no longer even a consumer of "sneakers." Now I'm a consumer of "runners shoes," and the only thing that will make me part with my first brand of runners shoes is if I discover a brand with yet another significant improvement, that is, a further specialization that once again raises my standard of desiring by being even more specialized to my needs (maybe, say, special runners shoes for over-40 guys to give greater cushioning for knee joints). 

This is true in any market. Offer a more specialized product when a large market is ready to subdivide into more specialized offerings, and you can easily make a killing. 

For example, this is true for those of you in this room who publish health newsletters. 

Where is the next big subdivision coming in the health newsletter field? Might it be a newsletter all about emerging cancer therapies and cures...and a guide to the top specialists in each? If you or a family member ever, heaven forbid, has cancer, would you hesitate for a nanosecond to buy such a newsletter to discover the doctors who are getting best results in treating that type of cancer? 

Or how about a newsletter just about arthritis? With the baby boomers, who comprise about one-fourth of the U.S. population, heading into their sixties and experiencing worse arthritis, could this be a star newsletter waiting to be born? 

There are some very big subdivisions coming in the health newsletter field. I'm not certain where they will be, but if you start looking closely at your market, you'll see some large bubbles of people ready to gravitate immediately to a further subdivision, a further specialization, within the general health newsletter field. 

Here's a good exercise. Whatever market you're in, imagine that you must break your main product into more-specialized offerings. What would you come up with? Try this exercise, and you'll spot some red-hot contenders most likely to be your next big product breakthroughs. 

All it requires of you is to take a broad product into a new, more specialized version that you suspect a lot of your customers would welcome. 

If you're the first to come out with such a specialized product, you may well grab the lion's share of money waiting for the first person who opens that door. Whatever market you're in, many people are waiting at this moment to rush through that door and hand you their money as they do. _Open the door for them!_ 

Many opportunities will arise for you once you know this characteristic of human desires— _they subdivide from the general to the more specialized._ 

- 452 - 

That's how desires operate in humans. But what are the specific desires that are behind virtually all of our actions? 

Over the years I've developed a handy checklist. 

Now, before I give you this checklist, let me remind you about the way I structure advertising. The best "formula" for a headline that I always strive for is a strong promise joined at the hip with powerful proof. 

I mention this again because many copywriters think the road to big increases in response is to merely address the bald desires of the market. In an uncluttered advertising world, that would be fine. And it was the best approach in the old days of salesmanship, before we all became inundated with daily tidal waves of marketing messages, many of which try to manipulate our emotions. 

So we've become wary of the "purely emotional" approach and demand proof if we are to respond. 

With that as a caveat, that the following desires are _not_ the sole keys to response, that they must always be accompanied by powerful proof, here then is my checklist of the most-motivating human emotions. 

**==> picture [263 x 195] intentionally omitted <==**

This checklist is very helpful to make sure you're touching all the bases that your product may address for your prospects. They all begin with the letter "R," and I call them the ten "Rs" of desire... 

_1. Recognition._ This includes things like respect, fame, exclusivity, prestige, popularity, and status. Always go through this checklist and ask, for example, "How can my product enhance the recognition, respect, prestige, fame, or status of my prospect?" Go through the entire list of 10, and you'll often come up with several hot buttons you weren't pressing. 

- 4 5 3 - 

But remember to press these hot buttons gracefully, discreetly, so you don't seem as if you're being overtly manipulative in your appeal to emotion. Let me give you a quick example. Recently I wrote a campaign for a high-end cruise aboard the magnificent four-masted schooner, the _Sea Cloud._ This is the most elegant, beautiful, and luxurious private sailing yacht in the world, built by Wall Street tycoon E. F. Hutton and his wife, Marjorie Merriweather Post, the Post cereal heiress. 

One of the photos we featured in the brochure was of this great ship entering a picturesque harbor. The copy _could_ have said, "You'll feel so proud to be a passenger aboard such a magnificent ship, the envy of every other ship in the harbor." 

Yes, this does appeal to the person's desire for recognition, status, and prestige, but it's too blatant. It can too easily be dismissed by the reader, because he or she does _not_ want to be someone who needs to be envied. 

When appealing to people's emotions, it often pays to be a little less obvious, such as this caption I wrote under a photo of the ship entering a picturesque European port... 

_"Visiting the picturesque harbors of your journey, whether Barcelona, Corsica, or Nice, you will not be able to suppress a feeling of pride as the_ Sea Cloud, _the largest and most elegant private yacht in the world, glides gracefully past all other ships, turning all heads."_ 

See the difference? The first way is too blatant. It makes the reader feel, "Oh, you think I'm someone who wants to show off my status? Well, you've got me pegged wrong." 

The second way is subtle enough to appeal to this same emotion—to be recognized as special— _without_ being so obvious and thus triggering your prospect's denial of having such crass emotions. In other words, unless you're selling a secret decoder ring to eight-year-old boys, you _don't_ want to use the words _"Impress Your Friends!"_ 

With all of these desires, find a skillful, graceful way to tap into them without being so obvious that you make your prospect step back and say, _"No, that's not me. I'm not someone driven by such emotions."_ 

_2. Rejuvenation._ This incorporates longevity, health, fitness, having lots of energy, even eternal life, all of which are universal desires. Think of all these concepts when reviewing your copy, to see if you can work in any appeals to "rejuvenation." 

_3. Relaxation._ This includes fun, leisure, having the sheer _luxury of time_ to do 

- 4 5 4 - 

whatever you'd like for a while. Remember when you were a kid and had a whole Saturday—or summer—to do whatever you liked? What a luxury! Today most of us would consider it a luxury to be able to read a magazine cover to cover without interruption. Without stretching the case, try to find a way to promise that your product can help your prospect enjoy more convenience, leisure, free time, fun, freedom from worry, etc. 

_**4. Relief** from_ pain, shame, guilt, or difficulty of any sort. Go through this checklist and see if your product can touch on any of those. 

_**5. Religion.**_ By this I mean any strong set of beliefs. We all, especially in our passionate interests, have a built-in set of beliefs about that topic. 

For example, I have strong beliefs about what good advertising is. If somebody's going to sell me something about advertising, they should mention David Ogilvy, John Caples, and the other stars we've talked about. They're the patron saints of my advertising religion. If you're selling marketing information and you mention those names to me, I instantly feel that you and I are on the same wave length, and I'm much more open to buying what you sell. 

Whatever market you write to, people in that market are wearing sunglasses, or filters—the filters of their strong beliefs through which they see and judge everything. Your copy cannot change these filters, and if you contradict or go against them, you will lose the sale. Much better to (1) know what their belief filters are and (2) show how your product or service confirms, expresses, and enhances their most strongly held beliefs. 

_**6. Remuneration.**_ Make sure you tell your prospects how your product makes or saves them money, advances their career, increases their success, expands their power to do or be something, or helps them gain financial independence. 

_7._ _**Results.**_ People strongly desire to see specific, measurable improvements in key areas of their lives. That's a very gratifying thing to experience. Tell how your product makes it happen. 

_8. Revenge._ When I see this one, I have to laugh. I'm Scottish on my mother's side and Italian on my father's side. In some Italian families, revenge is a point of honor. On my father's side, I had many uncles, some of them colorful characters. All of them have passed away now, but as they got older, my aunts would accuse them of having _Italian Alzheimer's_ —they forget everything except their grudges! 

But despite popular movies like _The Godfather,_ this is not just an Italian thing. We _all_ remember and resent anyone who has slighted us or put us down. And this is a very strong and often-overlooked motivator. 

## For every piece of copy that I write, I go through this 10-point desire checklist

- 4 5 5 - 

to make sure I'm not missing any one of these motivating desires. 

How to work in revenge? Evoke in the reader's mind a commonly experienced time or place when they did not feel successful, respected, loved, beautiful, thin, whatever...and sell against that feeling. Vividly and sensitively review how well you know the slights and wounds they've experienced at the hands of others. "This is why your success will taste all the sweeter once they and everyone else in your world encounter the new you. _You will show them how wrong they were about you."_ 

Revenge is the powerful psychology behind such famous headlines as _"They laughed when I sat down at the piano, but when I started to play..."_ The psychology is "You belittled me once. Do you see how wrong you were? Look what I've become." 

_**9. Role performance.**_ Here's another that's very often overlooked. We all want to perform better in our roles in life—be a better copywriter, parent, boss, lover, anything! This is a very strong emotion. Tie this desire to the ways your product helps your prospect be better in performing his or her roles. 

_**10. And finally, romance.**_ This includes attraction, beauty, sex, adventure, curiosity, travel, stimulation of any kind. We all have a romantic soul to some extent, and that, too, is a powerful emotional benefit we often overlook. 

Always go through this checklist and see which ones can apply, and you will invariably find more than you thought at first. 

## **"The Battle Is Won Before It Is Engaged"** 

Now let's talk about fulfilling _your_ most strongly held desires. Let's go back to what I mentioned when we started this seminar. So much of my philosophy in life, as a Zen master might say, is that you want to see your target before you let your arrow fly. If you're going to _hit_ a target, you must first _have_ a target! Likewise, General Sun Tzu said that the battle is won before it is engaged. 

All of this means that with any activity you enter into, you want to have in your mind— _before you begin the activity_ —a clear, vivid picture of the success you want to experience. This will help you so much in realizing the success you desire. 

All too often we just plunge ahead without even envisioning the successful outcome we want to achieve. 

This holds true for your life in general. So many people go through life just wanting to have a successful, happy, achievement-filled life. But year after year goes by, and they're not very satisfied. They don't get anyplace. It's because they lack a clear-cut destination and a specific plan for getting there. 

- 4 5 6 - 

It's as if you were to go into an airport and say to the ticket agent, "I want to go someplace great. I really do. I want to really experience a wonderful journey." 

But the ticket agent can't help you unless you say _specifically_ where you want to go. If you say, "No, I'm having trouble choosing. There are so many choices that I can't decide yet on a specific destination. But I do really want it to be something great..." In this case, the ticket agent cannot help you. You're not going to get anywhere. 

If, on the other hand, you say, "I want to go to San Francisco," then the ticket agent can give you a ticket to get to San Francisco, you can board the plane, take action to follow your plan, and you'll arrive in San Francisco. 

It's the same way in life. If you want to arrive at a terrific destination, you must first have one! 

If you're not being specific about exactly what you'd like to experience in your life, you're like that undecided traveler who goes to the airport and shies away from asking for a specific ticket. You must decide _specifically_ where you want to go, what you want to achieve in life, and then envision experiencing it. Maybe it's not going to be the same thing five years from now, and that's fine. That's no excuse for not having a destination now. Life changes, goals change, and that's part of the process. As J. P. Morgan advised, "Go as far as you can see; when you get there, you'll be able to see farther." 

But as of right now, you must take that first step toward that first specific destination, one that lights up your life, that makes you enthusiastic about getting up in the morning because you know you're making daily progress toward something wonderful in your life. 

It all starts with a clear vision of what you want, of something that really excites you. 

But what do you do if you have no idea of what you'd like to experience in life? 

Make _discovering your passion_ your first big goal, your first major destination. Imagine seeing yourself feeling so happy because you have finally discovered what you want to do, where you'd like to do it, and with whom you'd like to do it. Let that be your first destination, and once you arrive there, plan your next destination. _"Go as far as you can see. Then you '11 see further."_ 

In other words, whether you _are_ feeling fairly sure of what you'd like to achieve in your life...or you _are not...the_ process works the same way. If you're not sure, make finding out your first goal. If you are fairly sure, follow the same 

- 4 5 7 - 

process I'll now share... 

## **The Four-Part Secret to Achieving Success at Anything in Life, Including Copywriting, Marketing, and Accumulating Significant Wealth** 

There is a simple four-part process for succeeding in life or in a marketing project or arriving in San Francisco. 

_First,_ you must have a clear definition of your destination. You want to be very clear in answering the question "Where do I want to go, what do I want to be, or what do I want to experience from this activity?" 

_Second,_ ask, "What is my plan for getting there?" 

_**Third,**_ you must take action to follow your plan. If you want to wind up in San Francisco, you need a plan for getting there, a plan that includes buying a ticket and getting on the plane. 

_**And fourth,**_ every day you must review your plan to self-correct and stay on course or to get back on course if you've strayed. Every day you must remind yourself of the first three simple steps of this formula for each major goal you're pursuing, so you can correct your progress. 

## **The Two Reasons Why Most People Don't Achieve Their Goals in Life** 

All four steps of this process are critical for every major goal you want to achieve in every area of your life. 

You see, there are two reasons why most people don't achieve their goals in life. 

First, they don't have a specific destination. As the great sales trainer and motivational speaker Zig Ziglar puts it, most people are _"wandering generalities, not meaningful specifics."_ 

And second, even among those who start with a clear destination, they are too easily blown off course. Remember, even an airplane on its way from New York to San Francisco doesn't travel in a laser-beam-straight line. It may run into storms. It might have to avoid a tornado somewhere in the Midwest or just be temporarily blown off course by high winds. 

But just like a good pilot, if you have a clear, specific destination _**and you regularly (daily) review your destination and plan for getting there,**_ **you'll** get 

- 458 - 

right back on track and will, in fact, wind up in San Francisco. 

This is so important. How often does it happen to all of us, even if we start out with the best of intentions with a very specific destination, that a storm comes up and we get distracted, blown off our course. The key difference in those who succeed is that they have an automatic, daily self-correcting mechanism, which means that if you daily review your destination and your plan for getting there, you'll be reminded to get back on track as quickly as you can. 

Too many people, once their plane gets blown off course, say, gets turned south instead of west, will just keep heading south for the rest of their lives because they didn't remember to review their destination and get back on course. 

This is what I urge you to do—to put in place in your life a simple, short part of each day where you review your various destinations for each major part of your life—spiritual, health, family, financial, professional, every area that's important to you. 

The whole process may seem daunting, but it's really simple, and you can work on just one goal at a time until you have each area of your life planned out. 

First, just be sure you have a destination or goal that you want to reach for each of the key areas of your life—spiritual, health, family, wealth, career, every area that's important to you. 

Then map out a plan for getting there. 

Then start taking action to execute your plan. 

And then every day review your progress to make sure you're staying on course. 

Again, all of this is not just about marketing. It's about how you can become a master of desire, of your own desires, of knowing how to fulfill your own wishes and dreams in your life. This four-part process is very powerful and is what has worked for me. 

Something else I've learned is that all achievement is so much easier when you harness the power of your subconscious mind. 

## **How to Harness Your Mighty Subconscious Mind to Make Your Dreams Come True with an Ease and Power That Will Astonish You** 

You already know that your mind has two parts. You have a conscious mind and a subconscious mind. Generally we use only about 10 percent of our very powerful subconscious minds. Perhaps even less. 

- 459 - 

My interest throughout my life has been this: is there a way to make life easier by tapping more into our subconscious minds? 

One of the examples I mentioned yesterday was to think, right before you go to bed, about a solution that you're trying to find or a problem you're trying to solve, and just ask your very powerful computer, your subconscious mind, to think about this overnight. Picture an image of a mighty giant. Picture a big, strong, friendly male giant if you're a man, and a beautiful, wise, larger-than-life, loving female giant if you're a woman. This attractive, powerful, friendly, loving giant is really _you,_ that is, your subconscious mind. 

Tell your friendly, loving giant, "If I can get an answer on this by tomorrow morning, I'd like it." Then just drop it, let it go. Don't give it any more conscious thought. You'll be amazed at how often the answer, a brilliant answer, is waiting for you the next day, as soon as you awaken. 

Sometimes, your friendly giant, your subconscious mind, will answer you in the morning with another question. In effect, he or she is saying, "Master, I'd like to solve this problem for you, but I need this bit of information." 

And you'll know what to look for next. 

**==> picture [291 x 193] intentionally omitted <==**

To understand how to use both your conscious and subconscious mind properly, there's a simple analogy we can look at. 

Imagine that the airplane in this picture represents you and your great, Godgiven ability to soar to your highest abilities, to fly to fantastic destinations of your choosing in your life. 

Your _conscious_ mind is the pilot that does the steering of the plane and works the controls. But your subconscious is the rest of the plane that provides all the 

- 4 6 0 - 

lift, the power, the dramatic propulsion for the entire aircraft. It's a tremendously powerful machine. 

Not understanding this, we very often try to get to where we're going just by using our conscious minds—in effect, having the pilot drag the plane. Of course, that's not the best use of your conscious mind. When you get very intense over something, when you press too hard and try too hard, it's because you're pressuring yourself consciously to get something done. 

Perhaps, for example, you're being pressured by a deadline. This can unwittingly force you into making a big mistake in using your aircraft, a mistake by which you, as the pilot, are feeling so stressed and anxious, you climb out of your cockpit and try to drag the plane where you want to go. Feeling pressured, you start exerting too much conscious control over the process. 

Whether you have a deadline or not, whether you're feeling pressured or not, the smartest way to respond is to stay calmly in control in the cockpit and use your conscious mind the way it should be used, not to supply the raw power, but rather to ignite the vast propulsion that is possible in that jet engine that is your subconscious mind. That is the proper use—the correct roles—of both your conscious and subconscious mind. 

OK, so how do you do that? 

**==> picture [262 x 195] intentionally omitted <==**

Harnessing the awesome power of your subconscious mind starts simply by realizing that you possess it. You must know that you have within you this friendly, loving giant who wants nothing more than to serve your every command. I have a phrase I like to use. You have within you a _**bashful genie.**_ 

- 4 6 1 - 

You have a bashful genie within you, otherwise known as your subconscious mind. It's a very, very powerful genie. But it is also bashful. 

It's bashful because your powerful genie is very sensitive to criticism— exquisitely sensitive, almost like a little child. If it feels criticized, it's going to whoosh back into its bottle, close the cork, and not come out. 

Why is your genie so bashful? 

Its highest mission in life is to protect you from harm, including criticism and disappointment, and it will resist participating in anything that may bring you harm, including self-criticism, chastisement, guilt, or disappointment that your conscious mind may inflict. Its main job is to protect you at all times. And if it fears punishment coming or retribution or guilt, it seals off to defend you. 

So if you want your subconscious to bravely emerge from its bottle, to breathe the fresh air of freedom, feel its awesome strength, and express its majestic power on your behalf, you must assure your bashful genie that there is _nothing to fear in coming out to help you._ There will be no negatives involved, no downside, no judgmental criticism regarding anything about its performance, no selfchastisements if deadlines are missed. Complete, unconditional acceptance, meaning a complete absence of self-criticism and judgment, is the most important message to communicate to your inner genie. 

## **Acceptance Is the Essence of Love and the Key to Unleashing Your Subconscious Mind's Power** 

Let your inner, bashful genie know that your _conscious_ mind will concern itself with deadlines and other forms of external pressure. Your inner genie doesn't have to worry about any of that in the least. 

If you want to harness your subconscious mind as never before, please listen to me carefully on this. What I am teaching here is radically different from what most people recommend for goal setting, and it's a critically important distinction. It will make all the difference in the world in achieving your dreams. 

Others may tell you to be sure to give yourself a deadline for each of your goals, to hold yourself strictly accountable as to whether you are meeting your goal schedule, to push yourself relentlessly to meet these deadlines, and to lash yourself with the whip of self-discipline if you're not. And all of this will make your inner genie whoosh right back into its bottle. 

In my own experience, I've found all this counterproductive, and I believe it's the main reason people don't want to even attempt big dreams. _Their subconscious_ — _their mighty, bashful genie_ — _is afraid of disappointment and thus won't_ 

## 4 6 2 -

_-_ 

_even make the attempt!_ 

You must remove the fear of disappointment. Even if you don't succeed, you are so much better off for having made the attempt! At least you will have learned what not to do and can make another attempt from there. If you want your friendly, loving giant to feel safe and come out of its bottle to serve and help you, you must take away all fear of making the attempt to achieve such a big goal. Here's how... 

## **How to Free Your "Bashful Genie" to Fulfill Your Commands** 

You're going to make a deal with your genie, your subconscious mind, your bashful genie. You're going to clearly picture your subconscious mind as a big, friendly, loving giant, and say, "Let's make a deal. You're my best friend in life. I ask that you help me achieve the goal I will now describe, a goal I'd love to experience. But please know that _no matter what happens, it's OK!_ If we don't make it together, it's really OK. There will be no downside whatsoever in our attempt. Just knowing we tried makes me feel so proud of both of us, and regardless of the outcome, I'd like to know that you helped me. Is that OK with you?" 

Then picture your big, loving, friendly genie smiling and saying, "Yes, Master. Absolutely! You can count on me! Just tell me what you want." 

And then, using vivid mental pictures as if your goal is already achieved, tell your inner genie exactly what you want. After you do, repeat the deal you've made, as follows... 

"Remember, Inner Genie, no matter what happens, I love you, I accept you, we will always be the best of friends, and nothing will ever change that. There is nothing to fear in pursuing this goal. No matter what happens, the fact that we are pursuing this goal with energy and determination is what's most important. If it doesn't materialize, that's OK too. I will not beat us up over it. I am so proud of both of us just for making the attempt at such a glorious goal. So let's give this everything we've got and make the following picture come true." 

And then you once again hold in your mind exactly what you'd like to experience, _as if you 're already experiencing it in vivid detail right now in the present._ 

You'll be surprised at how much new force now bursts forth from your subconscious mind, because now there's no penalty. You will have freed your subconscious mind from the fear of disappointment and unleashed your greatest 

- 463 - 

inner powers. 

## **Here Are the Rules for Harnessing Your Bashful Genie, Your Friendly, Loving, Inner Giant** 

Now let's review the rules I've found to maximize the power of your subconscious mind, to let it really start flexing its muscles on your behalf... 

_1. Your bashful genie needs to feel safe to come out and play._ Your inner genie is very much like a massive computer controlled by a child. You have to treat your subconscious as a child in some ways, making sure its emotions do not feel threatened, or else it won't come out of its bottle and work for you. 

_2. Your bashful genie needs precise clarity about what you want._ You can't say to the ticket agent at the airport, "I want a ticket to someplace great." That's not something the ticket agent can give you. 

Your inner genie is just like the ticket agent. You have to say very specifically where you want to go, what you want to experience. 

For example, if you want to make $100,000 a year, you don't say, "I want to make a lot of money." You say, "I picture myself making $100,000 a year." 

And don't even give it a deadline. All you have to do is say, "I picture myself making $100,000 a year." 

If you want to make $500,000 dollars a year, say, "I picture myself making $500,000 a year." 

You might wonder, "Why not just ask for a trillion?" 

The answer is that each law of the universe has to work in harmony with the other laws. And certain things are not going to happen because, they contradict the laws of the universe. 

For example, we are holding this seminar in the beautiful rooftop penthouse of the St. Regis Hotel, some 20 stories above the sidewalks of New York. No matter how vividly I may imagine success, no matter how I may harness my subconscious mind, if my goal is to jump out this window and fly unaided by any mechanical device and land as lightly as a sparrow on East 55th Street, that's not going to happen. It's not in harmony with the laws of the universe. 

Likewise, if I want to get into the ring with a heavyweight boxer, whatever I may say to myself beforehand, I will likely be knocked out, dead, or running away screaming within 10 seconds, as I am not trained or physically qualified to pursue that goal. It's not something I would ever want to do anyway. 

- 464 - 

So a goal has to be within the realm of the other laws of the universe. It has to be possible for _someone_ to achieve. And it should also be something you truly want. Your own desires are usually a reliable guide to what you can likely achieve. There's an old saying, _"If you want it, it wants you."_ 

Depending on your current comfort level of asking for big things in life, you may set your yearly income goal somewhere between $100,000 and a trillion dollars. The higher your comfort level with setting big goals, the higher your number will be. But the main thing to remember is, don't let your fear of disappointment shrink the size of your goal. From now on, you should set goals _without_ fear of disappointment, and this will make a big difference in the size of the goals you go after and achieve. 

This is the whole purpose of removing the fear of disappointment from the goal-setting process, of making it perfectly OK with yourself if the goal is not reached. When you make this pact with your bashful genie that no matter what happens—even if you miss the goal—it was nevertheless thrilling to make the attempt, then everything will be fine regardless of the outcome, and you will have achieved far more than if you had never set the goal to begin with. 

So don't shrink your goal to fit your fear of disappointment. Greatly enlarge it by removing any fear of disappointment. By taking this view, you free yourself up to set and achieve much bigger goals. 

In effect, you are saying to yourself, "Why not try for something spectacular, something that electrifies me with excitement just to consider it a possibility, however remote? And if I don't achieve it, so what? What have I lost in shooting for it? Nothing! So let me act as if it is possible for me to achieve and then go all out for it." This thrilling pursuit of a spectacular goal will, in itself, add indescribable zest and sparkle to your life. What you'll learn, often to your astonishment, is that once you consider it possible and go all out, without the fear of disappointment, you very often _do_ achieve it—or even surpass it! And if you don't, you still will have achieved great things and learned a great deal in the attempt. So either way, you're a winner. 

So don't be at all afraid of setting goals that are so big and ambitious, they are absolutely thrilling to you, and you can do that now because you are no longer tempering them by the fear of disappointment. 

I'm repeating this here because it's such a critical point and one that keeps the majority of people from setting big goals, dreaming big dreams, and achieving spectacular successes. 

## Remember, you're banishing any fear of disappointment, because this keeps

- 4 6 5 - 

you from even trying. You will never again let the size of your goal be determined by the size of your fear of disappointment. You are removing the fear of disappointment from the calculation of what would be thrilling for you to experience in life and also from the pursuit of that very goal. 

If you don't achieve this amazing, thrilling, wonderful goal, _hey, it s OK! It really is! Nothing to beat yourself up over. To the contrary, you have covered yourself in glory just by deciding to make such a daring attempt. The daring attempt itself adds so much zest to your life and takes you so much further than if you had never attempted it at all._ That's the new deal you're making with yourself. 

Paradoxically, by removing the fear of disappointment, you will multiply your chances of succeeding exponentially. And you will be astonished at how often you do achieve or even surpass goals that seemed outrageously beyond reach before. 

You are intentionally setting your goals way beyond your familiar comfort zone. You are intentionally pushing the envelope of what you thought could be possible for you, because now you have no fear of discomfort if you do happen to fall short. By all odds, you will be _much_ closer to your wildly ambitious goal than if you had never pursued it at all! 

And that's the critical distinction I'm making today. You're allowing it to be OK _not_ to reach whatever goal you want. There's no disappointment, there's nothing to lose, so set a fantastic goal that, if you did achieve it, would make you feel on top of the world. And ask for your mighty inner genie to help you get there. 

Even if you think it's onlyl percent possible, that's OK. If it's humanly possible for _somebody_ in your position to do this, go for it! Using the words I gave you before, tell your subconscious mind that there's no downside. If we don't make it, great, we gave it a shot and that in itself is wonderful. 

_**3. Your bashful genie understands only the now.**_ As part of unleashing the tremendous power of your inner genie, remember that, like a child, it understands only the now. 

This means that the best way to give your inner genie the directions is, as I said before, to vividly imagine the accomplishment of your goal _as if it's already taking place in the now._ Vividly see, hear, touch, taste, and smell every detail of living your dream as if it's already happening, and your subconscious will get the message loud and clear that this is what you want to manifest. 

If you want to make $100,000 a year—or $500,000—picture yourself already having done it, as if it's happening right now, and how great that makes you feel. 

- 4 6 6 - 

Let's say your goal is to visit San Francisco. Don't just use the words "San Francisco" to communicate with your inner genie. Using vivid mental imagery, picture yourself in San Francisco. See yourself dining at a fine restaurant overlooking the bay. What are you eating? What are you drinking? What are you thinking at that moment? Picture it all! Feel the rumble as you ride a cable car and hear its bell ring out the stops. Smell the tang of seafood in the air as you tour Fisherman's Wharf. Feel the mist on your face as you walk up a steep hill in the foggy early morning and come upon a panoramic view of the Golden Gate Bridge. 

These mental sights, sounds, and experiences tell your inner genie—in vivid, sensual snapshots—exactly what you want to experience. These vivid mental images are the language of your subconscious. With them, your inner genie will fully understand what you want and will then come up with all kinds of plans and suggestions to manifest those same experiences in real life. 

But you must imagine these things as if _they 're already happening now,_ because your subconscious mind understands only the now. If you say to your inner genie, _someday_ I want to experience this, your subconscious mind, which is extremely literal, will interpret this to mean that you don't want these things right away, that you want to have them only at some distant date in the future. And, to your literal subconscious mind, if it's told to keep something in the future, that's what it will do—make sure it never happens in the present but always keep putting it off for the future, which is not what you want. 

## **How I Have Applied This Goal-Setting Process to My Copywriting Assignments** 

So, for example, when I was writing direct mail packages, before doing any research, I would first see in my mind exactly what I wanted to experience. For instance, I would imagine my client phoning me, saying, "Gary, you did it, you broke the record for response, you beat the control by 50 percent! Congratulations. This is just the beginning of the work we're going to be doing together. I'm so pleased with these results, I just had to call you." 

To my surprise at first, almost the exact conversation I would envision in my own mind would often be played back to me months later— _by my client!_ I suspect that my clear envisioning of it beforehand had a lot to do with it. 

In my written proposals to clients, I would explain, using _The Persuasion Equation®,_ that this is what I understand you're looking for and why it's important to you. I would, as I explained before, then walk them through why I believed I was uniquely qualified to fulfill this desire for them. I would prove it with a 

- 467 - 

mountain of proof—testimonials, successful case histories of results achieved for similar clients, samples of my work for others, etc. And then I would spell out how we would succeed together on the assignment. I would spell out the painstaking amount of research I would dive into—how I will write no less than 25 headlines before choosing the best...how I will investigate the greatest successes of others in the same market and will harness the same powerful elements for them...how I will search thoroughly for the most powerful premiums...how I will present an array of seductive offers for us to test...and so on. 

And then, as the coup de grace, I would add that a critical step is to apply my mental technique of clearly envisioning our success together. I would explain that this is not a guarantee of success, but before starting any assignment, I vividly picture in my mind what I want to achieve for my client, as I have found that doing this helps to bring it about. 

I would tell them that I paint a vivid picture to inspire me, a mental movie of mail trucks pulling up to your office building and unloading bags and bags full of checks. I picture you calling me with the wonderful news that we've got a powerful new control package, and we are both delighted at that news. I picture that the new campaign is so strong, it adds significant new pricing power in case you'd like to raise prices. It builds your house list as no other package before and is the talk of the industry. 

I even picture your customers writing in to say how much they enjoyed reading such a clear and persuasive presentation of your product, that it really hooked them and they even showed it to their spouse. I picture the editor (if it's a book or newsletter) or others involved in making the product telling you that never before has anyone so clearly and convincingly captured this product's essence and explained so persuasively why it's needed by everyone in this marketplace. 

And I would go on for a few more sentences, painting with vivid images exactly what my client would _love_ to experience. This extremely powerful copy made my proposals irresistible. I almost never failed to win the assignment, and I believe that this envisioning section of my proposals had a lot to do with it, as it created visions of grandeur dancing in the heads of my clients. Once a client saw such visions in his own mind, and I was the one who put them there, how could he possibly snatch the assignment from me in favor of someone else and risk losing all these delightful developments he had just glimpsed? 

And, almost always, this is what I was then able to manifest for my clients, as these visions unfolded just as I and he had imagined. Once you start harnessing your subconscious mind in this way, you will be astonished at how closely it 

- 468 - 

manifests in the material world what you so clearly envisioned in your mind. 

And this is the best way to achieve whatever you want— _**it happens in mind before it happens in fact.**_ The Super Bowl is won before the players take the field. That's how it's won. They picture themselves celebrating in the locker room. They picture the game over and that they've beaten the other team. 

Now what if _both_ teams picture this same outcome? Then other factors, namely talent and preparation, will carry the day. But most athletes, like most people, do _not_ practice this habit. So you will give yourself a tremendous edge by doing so. 

The point is, you will succeed so much more often by setting your goal, your destination, and then living out that vision by letting your mighty subconscious mind, your awesomely powerful inner genie, be freed from his bottle, freed from the fear of disappointment because that is your agreement, that even if you don't succeed together, it's OK. There is no disappointment, no blame, no hurt. The glory is in the pact that you will give it your all together. 

This means that you need never again downsize your dreams to protect yourself from disappointment. Dispense with fear of disappointment, and you can supersize your dreams and achieve more than you have ever imagined before. 

When your subconscious knows this and also knows specifically where you want to go, it will come up with all kinds of suggestions that you might not have thought of consciously. 

If you're a football team applying this, as Vince Lombardi demonstrated so well, because he used these methods too, you harness your subconscious to make snap decisions with a computer-like speed and precision that your conscious mind could never achieve. 

That's how a great runner makes touchdowns. He doesn't consciously, at every moment when he's running, look and painstakingly analyze the pros and cons of running this way or that. If he did, he'd be tackled immediately for a loss. 

Instead, he frees his subconscious to help him run like the fox away from the hounds, to get him to touchdown turf in whatever path will take him there, making split-second decisions all along the way in keeping with his goal to score a touchdown. 

And that's the formula. The conscious mind says, "I want a touchdown. Subconscious mind, I'm handing you the ball, and you take over from here!" 

And just as the fullback makes instantaneous decisions through his subconscious to step this way, spin that way, cut back here, dodge a tackier there, 

- 4 6 9 - 

and so on, likewise in your life, once you've engaged your subconscious as I've recommended, you will find yourself getting ideas you never had before, sensing intuitions that lead you to breakthroughs, following up on hunches and opportunities you may have noticed before and that prove to be turning points in your career. 

You discover that you are much "luckier" than you ever were before, effortlessly coming upon insights, networking contacts, and mutual acquaintances that help you in scores of amazing ways you could never have consciously orchestrated. All because you have learned how to fly—by letting your conscious mind be the pilot and your subconscious mind—your awesomely powerful but bashful inner genie—be your mighty jet engine or, perhaps I should say, _your magic carpet._ 

## **Step Four in Unleashing Your Bashful Genie** 

OK, just to review the three steps we've covered so far... 

_1. Your bashful genie needs to feel safe to come out and play,_ so, just for the fun of it and with no fear of disappointment, you are going to try for an outrageous goal. 

_2. Your bashful genie needs precise clarity about what you want._ 

_3. Your bashful genie understands only the now, so envision your goal as if it's already achieved._ 

And finally... 

_4. Your bashful genie needs daily reminding._ As I mentioned before, all airplanes get blown off course, usually by a little, sometimes a lot. But since a good pilot keeps his or her destination in mind at all times, he or she corrects for this and is back on course in no time. 

You must do the same. The way to be sure you do is with a daily review of your goals. Just as with the pilot, when you have written down a very clear definition of where you want to go, it's easy to keep reminding yourself every day that this is what you want. I'll show you a remarkably easy way to do this in a moment, the method I use. 

## **One Final Bit of Advice... Dream Big!** 

Your bashful genie, when motivated correctly as I've explained above, can achieve almost anything. Don't waste a NASA-size computer doing basic arithmetic. Set a _big, thrilling_ goal that's worthy of you, that electrifies you and 

- 470 - 

has the power to give you the big, exciting life you want for yourself! 

## **Of Elephants and Fleas...and the Human Mind** 

There was once a reporter whose editor told him to go out and do a story on the circus that had just come to town. He was told to be sure to check how the animals were being treated, as this had become a controversial subject, how circuses treat their animals. 

He had never seen a circus before, so he went behind the scenes. He walked over to where the elephants were kept and noticed something strange. He saw that all the elephants, both large and small, were tethered to stakes in the ground. What was strange, though, was that the adult elephants were tethered by a thin rope, not much thicker than a clothesline. 

Yet the baby elephants were tethered with a thick chain attached to a very heavy iron stake. 

The reporter asked one of the handlers, "Don't you guys have this backward? Don't the big elephants need the heavy chains and the babies only the rope?" 

The handler said that, no, that's not how it works. "We have to put the heavy chain on the baby elephant's leg because elephants, even babies, are very strong. 

"As a baby, an elephant is curious, rambunctious, and wants to wander around. We can't let him do that because he might hurt himself or somebody else. So that chain is needed because he doesn't know his limitations yet. He'll pull hard on that chain. He'll yank it for all he's worth. 

"But in time, after enough struggles against that chain, he'll learn that he's not going anywhere. After that, for the rest of his life, all we need is a little rope. As soon as he sees that on his leg, he'll never even try to get away. He knows it's no use. That's why the big elephants have the little ropes on them. They've been so conditioned that their limitation is defined by that thing around their ankle, they'll never try to go anywhere as long as it's attached." 

When we hear that tale, we feel sorry for elephants in captivity. But we humans have ropes on us too. They're invisible, but they hold us in place as surely as the elephants'. 

All of us have tapes that play in our minds, tapes perhaps recorded originally by people who didn't believe in what we could achieve, or perhaps by people who had problems and disappointments in their own lives that they put onto us, chained around our ankles. All of us remember being belittled and mocked by others, especially by other children but sometimes even by adults who should have known better. But they didn't, and we can still hear their cutting remarks. We've all been 

- 4 7 1 - 

there in one way or another. 

So many times we've been wounded by criticism, and we made tapes out of hurtful remarks that we hear over and over again, sometimes subconsciously every time we are tempted to try, to push our envelope, to soar like the hawk, hunt like the tiger, or walk proudly and confidently in whatever direction we choose, like a wild elephant who's never been shackled. 

And even as we grew older and smarter and allowed ourselves to be educated in different and wonderful ways, we may never have shaken free of those chains on our ankles, those chains of doubt, insecurity, and inferiority that hold us in place. 

Well, guess what. You're grown up now, and what used to be chains are only thin ropes that you can easily snap free of! You have had the power for a long time. As I've tried to convey, you have _tremendous_ powers, far greater than an adult elephant! 

## **The Fleas Who Banged Their Heads Just Gave Up!** 

Fleas have incredible leaping ability. If you have ajar full of fleas and leave the jar open on top, soon you will have no fleas. They will have all leaped out. 

But if you were to put a lid on that jar of fleas and leave it for a couple days, something interesting happens. They don't like banging their heads every time they jump, so they will all have learned to jump much lower, low enough to avoid banging their little flea brains into the lid of the jar. 

And after that, they will leap only that high and no higher. You can take the lid off the jar, and they will still jump only so high, even though, just a few days ago, they could leap much higher. They've learned that this is their max, the highest they can jump without feeling pain, and, even after conditions change, won't jump any higher. 

Poor dumb fleas. But how often do we do the same? After we bang our heads on the lids placed above us, don't we often recalibrate our dreams and learn to jump just so high as to avoid getting hurt, just like a flea? 

Well, today you've learned how to avoid getting hurt by disappointment, by consciously removing it from consideration at the outset. This will make an enormous difference in your life, as you will see if you practice what I am recommending here. 

## **Three More Points to Remember** 

## Always keep your ambitious goal to yourself, because your decision to dream

- 472 - 

a big dream will sometimes threaten others, who may then discourage or ridicule your goal. So keep it to yourself unless you're partnering with someone who'd like to buy into a big dream too, as I encouraged my clients to do in my proposals. 

Always write it down. Writing something down somehow evokes its own magic in making something materialize.
